## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Thermoviscoelasticity
**Analysis**: This task belongs to the domain of thermoviscoelasticity, which studies the relationship between stress, strain, and temperature. The physical behavior of materials under various temperature conditions can be captured by the interplay between elastic and viscoelastic responses.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear elastic stress-strain relationship: sigma = c0 * epsilon (relationship between stress and strain under elastic deformation)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: E(T) = c0 + c1 * T (change in elastic modulus with temperature)
- Viscoelastic creep compliance: J(T) = c0 + c1 / T (temperature dependence of creep compliance in viscoelastic materials)
- Arrhenius equation for temperature-dependent relaxation time: tau = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (temperature dependence of relaxation time in viscoelastic materials)
- Thermal expansion coefficient: alpha = c0 + c1 * T (expansion of material with temperature)
- Viscoelastic model: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * integral(ep dt) (linear viscoelastic response to strain history)
- Non-Newtonian viscosity: mu = c0 * T**c1 (temperature dependence of viscosity in non-Newtonian fluids)
- Thermal conductivity: k = c0 + c1 * T (heat conduction in materials as a function of temperature)
- Specific heat capacity: c_p = c0 + c1 * T (heat capacity of a material as a function of temperature)
- Thermal diffusivity: alpha = k / (c_p * rho) (diffusion of heat in a material)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Anelastic relaxation → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x) in viscoelastic responses
- Hysteresis in cyclic loading → Cross-coupling between strain history and current stress in viscoelastic models
- Stress-strain hysteresis → Piecewise functions or rational fraction x/(1+x) for modeling cyclic behavior
- Temperature-dependent critical stress → Threshold/activation behavior (Max(x-c, 0)) for brittle-ductile transition
- Thermal expansion vs contraction → Variable products x*y for modeling complex thermal responses
- Viscoelastic stress relaxation → Power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2 for strain history effects on stress
- Thermal conductivity and diffusivity → Rational fraction x/(1+x) for heat conduction in materials
